It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\\n36:  *\\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. They're split\\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \\\"use strict\\\" code. The \\\"use strict\\\" bit is stored in\\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\\n48:  *\\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\\n50:  * different groups of flags:\\n51:  *\\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \\\"passed down\\\"\\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"are we parsing strict code?\\\", and so\\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\\n57:  * \\\"returned up\\\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"did we see a use strict\\n58:  * directive\\\"?\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\\n63:  *\\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\\n67:  * can be optimized away.\\n68:  *\\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\\n80:  *\\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \\\"pass-down\\\"\\n84:  * data and some \\\"return-up\\\" data.\\n85:  *\\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\\n90:  *\\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\\n93:  *\\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\\n96:  *\\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\\n99:  *\\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\\n103:  */\\n104: \\n105: class JSFunction;\\n106: class JSObject;\\n107: class JSScript;\\n108: struct It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\\n36:  *\\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. This is information conceptually \\\"passed down\\\"\\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"are we parsing strict code?\\\", and so\\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\\n55:  *\\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\\n57:  * \\\"returned up\\\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \\\"did we see a use strict\\n58:  * directive\\\"?\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\\n63:  *\\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\\n67:  * can be optimized away.\\n68:  *\\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\\n80:  *\\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \\\"pass-down\\\"\\n84:  * data and some \\\"return-up\\\" data.\\n85:  *\\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\\n99:  *\\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\\n101:  * `{ let a; let It stores\\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\\n44:  * character-type-agnostic. Certain limitations of\n24:  * C++ (primarily the inability to partially specialize function templates),\n25:  * plus the desire to minimize compiled code size in duplicate function\n26:  * template instantiations wherever possible, mean that Parser exhibits much of\n27:  * the same unholy template/inheritance complexity as token streams.\n28:  *\n29:  * == ParserSharedBase ==\n30:  *\n31:  * ParserSharedBase is the base class for both regular JS and BinAST parsing.\n32:  * This class contains common fields and methods between both parsers. There is\n33:  * currently no BinAST parser here so this can potentially be merged into the\n34:  * ParserBase type below.\n35:  *\n36:  * == ParserBase → ParserSharedBase, ErrorReportMixin ==\n37:  *\n38:  * ParserBase is the base class for regular JS parser, shared by all regular JS\n39:  * parsers of all character types and parse-handling behavior.  It stores\n40:  * everything character- and handler-agnostic.\n41:  *\n42:  * ParserBase's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n43:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| component, for all tokenizing aspects that are\n44:  * character-type-agnostic.  The character-type-sensitive components residing\n45:  * in |TokenStreamSpecific| (see the comment near the top of TokenStream.h)\n46:  * live elsewhere in this hierarchy.  These separate locations are the reason\n47:  * for the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameter to |TokenStreamChars| and\n48:  * |TokenStreamSpecific|.\n49:  *\n50:  * == PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> → ParserBase ==\n51:  *\n52:  * Certain parsing behavior varies between full parsing and syntax-only parsing\n53:  * but does not vary across source-text character types.  For example, the work\n54:  * to \"create an arguments object for a function\" obviously varies between\n55:  * syntax and full parsing but (because no source characters are examined) does\n56:  * not vary by source text character type.  Such functionality is implemented\n57:  * through functions in PerHandlerParser.\n58:  *\n59:  * Functionality only used by syntax parsing or full parsing doesn't live here:\n60:  * it should be implemented in the appropriate Parser<ParseHandler> (described\n61:  * further below).\n62:  *\n63:  * == GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> → PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler> ==\n64:  *\n65:  * Most parsing behavior varies across the character-type axis (and possibly\n66:  * along the full/syntax axis).  For example:\n67:  *\n68:  *   * Parsing ECMAScript's Expression production, implemented by\n69:  *     GeneralParser::expr, varies in this manner: different types are used to\n70:  *     represent nodes in full and syntax parsing (ParseNode* versus an enum),\n71:  *     and reading the tokens comprising the expression requires inspecting\n72:  *     individual characters (necessarily dependent upon character type).\n73:  *   * Reporting an error or warning does not depend on the full/syntax parsing\n74:  *     distinction.  But error reports and warnings include a line of context\n75:  *     (or a slice of one), for pointing out where a mistake was made.\n76:  *     Computing such line of context requires inspecting the source text to\n77:  *     make that line/slice of context, which requires knowing the source text\n78:  *     character type.\n79:  *\n80:  * Such functionality, implemented using identical function code across these\n81:  * axes, should live in GeneralParser.\n82:  *\n83:  * GeneralParser's most important field is the parser's token stream's\n84:  * |TokenStreamSpecific| component, for all aspects of tokenizing that (contra\n85:  * |TokenStreamAnyChars| in ParserBase above) are character-type-sensitive.  As\n86:  * noted above, this field's existence separate from that in ParserBase\n87:  * motivates the |AnyCharsAccess| template parameters on various token stream\n88:  * classes.\n89:  *\n90:  * Everything in PerHandlerParser *could* be folded into GeneralParser (below)\n91:  * if desired.  We don't fold in this manner because all such functions would\n92:  * be instantiated once per Unit -- but if exactly equivalent code would be\n93:  * generated (because PerHandlerParser functions have no awareness of Unit),\n94:  * it's risky to *depend* upon the compiler coalescing the instantiations into\n95:  * one in the final binary.  PerHandlerParser guarantees no duplication.\n96:  *\n97:  * == Parser<ParseHandler, Unit> final → GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit> ==\n98:  *\n99:  * The final (pun intended) axis of complexity lies in Parser.\n100:  *\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/firefox--871325b8@01dcdcebaca08ed5c32f8d50532752a063dc5ade/-/blob/js/src/frontend/Parser.h%3FL1-100"}}}

Compilation Chain\\n\\n## Overview\\nThe Firefox SpiderMonkey JavaScript engine compiles source code to bytecode through a multi-stage pipeline. This document traces the complete compilation path from source text to executable bytecode.\\n\\n## Stage 1: Compilation Entry Points\\n\\nThe public API for JavaScript compilation is exposed in `js/public/CompilationAndEvaluation.h` with the `JS::Compile()` family of functions. These are the user-facing entry points that accept JavaScript source text and return compiled `JSScript*` objects containing bytecode.\\n\\nFor advanced use cases without JSContext dependency, `js/public/experimental/CompileScript.h` provides the `JS::CompileGlobalScriptToStencil()` and related functions that work with a `FrontendContext` instead of `JSContext`, enabling off-thread compilation.\\n\\n## Stage 2: Compilation Driver (Frontend)\\n\\nThe high-level compilation logic is implemented in:\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.h`**: Declares compilation functions and compiler classes\\n- **`js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.cpp`**: Implements the compilation driver\\n\\nThe key compilation function is `CompileGlobalScript()` (exported in BytecodeCompiler.h), which is the implementation of the public `JS::Compile()` API. This driver orchestrates the parsing and bytecode emission pipeline.\\n\\nThe compiler uses template classes:\\n- `SourceAwareCompiler<Unit>`: Base class for all compilers\\n- `ScriptCompiler<Unit>`: For global and eval script compilation\\n- `ModuleCompiler<Unit>`: For module compilation\\n- `StandaloneFunctionCompiler<Unit>`: For function compilation\\n\\n## Stage 3: Tokenization\\n\\nBefore parsing can begin, source text must be tokenized. This is handled by:\\n- **`js/src/frontend/TokenStream.h`**: Token stream implementation\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Token.h`**: Token type definitions\\n- **`js/src/frontend/TokenKind.h`**: Token kind enumeration\\n\\nThe token stream parses the source character-by-character and generates tokens for the parser.\\n\\n## Stage 4: Parsing (AST Generation)\\n\\nThe JavaScript parser is a recursive-descent parser that generates an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST). Key files:\\n\\n**Parser Implementation:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Parser.h`**: Parser class hierarchy and declarations\\n- **`js/src/frontend/Parser.cpp`**: Complete parser implementation (line 7 contains documentation: \\\"JS parser. This is a recursive-descent parser for the JavaScript language specified by 'The ECMAScript Language Specification' (Standard ECMA-262)\\\")\\n\\nThe parser uses a complex template hierarchy to handle multiple character types (UTF-8 vs UTF-16) and parse modes (full parse vs. syntax parse):\\n- `ParserSharedBase`: Common base for all parsers\\n- `ParserBase`: Base for regular JS parsers\\n- `PerHandlerParser<ParseHandler>`: Handler-specific functionality\\n- `GeneralParser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Character-type-specific functionality\\n- `Parser<ParseHandler, Unit>`: Final parser with all specializations\\n\\n**Parse Node (AST) Types:**\\n- **`js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h`**: Defines all AST node types (lines 63-268 contain the `FOR_EACH_PARSE_NODE_KIND` macro listing all node types including EmptyStmt, ExpressionStmt, CallExpr, ArrayExpr, ObjectExpr, etc.)\\n- **`js/src/frontend/ParseNode.cpp`**: ParseNode implementation details\\n- **`js/src/frontend/FullParseHandler.h`**: Handler that creates full ParseNode trees\\n- **`js/src/frontend/SyntaxParseHandler.h`**: Handler for syntax-only parsing\\n\\nThe parser generates a tree of ParseNode objects representing the program structure.
